{"left":["\r\n","\r\n",{"c":0,"s":";;; -*- Mode: Emacs-Lisp; outline-regexp: \"\\n;;;;+\" -*-\r\n"},"\r\n",{"c":0,"s":";;;;;; Paredit: Parenthesis-Editing Minor Mode\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;;;;; Version 20\r\n"},"\r\n",{"c":0,"s":";;; This code is written by Taylor R. Campbell (except where explicitly\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; noted) and placed in the Public Domain. All warranties are\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; disclaimed.\r\n"},"\r\n",{"c":0,"s":";;; Add this to your .emacs after adding paredit.el to /path/to/elisp/:\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; (add-to-list 'load-path \"/path/to/elisp/\")\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; (autoload 'paredit-mode \"paredit\"\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; \"Minor mode for pseudo-structurally editing Lisp code.\"\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; t)\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; (add-hook '...-mode-hook (lambda () (paredit-mode +1)))\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; Usually the ... will be lisp or scheme or both. Alternatively, you\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; can manually toggle this mode with M-x paredit-mode. Customization\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; of paredit can be accomplished with `eval-after-load':\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; (eval-after-load 'paredit\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; '(progn ...redefine keys, &c....))\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; This should run in GNU Emacs 21 or later and XEmacs 21.5 or later.\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; It is highly unlikely to work in earlier versions of GNU Emacs, and\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; it may have obscure problems in earlier versions of XEmacs due to\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; the way its syntax parser reports conditions, as a result of which\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; the code that uses the syntax parser must mask *all* error\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; conditions, not just those generated by the syntax parser.\r\n"},"\r\n",{"c":0,"s":";;; This mode changes the keybindings for a number of simple keys,\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; notably (, ), \", \\, and ;. The bracket keys (round or square) are\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; defined to insert parenthesis pairs and move past the close,\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; respectively; the double-quote key is multiplexed to do both, and\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; also insert an escape if within a string; backslashes prompt the\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; user for the next character to input, because a lone backslash can\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; break structure inadvertently; and semicolons ensure that they do\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; not accidentally comment valid structure. (Use M-; to comment an\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; expression.) These all have their ordinary behaviour when inside\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; comments, and, outside comments, if truly necessary, you can insert\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; them literally with C-q.\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; These keybindings are set up for my preference. One particular\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; preference which I've seen vary greatly from person to person is\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; whether the command to move past a closing delimiter ought to\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; insert a newline. Since I find this behaviour to be more common\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; than that which inserts no newline, I have ) bound to it, and the\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; more involved M-) to perform the less common action. This bothers\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; some users, though, and they prefer the other way around. This\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; code, which you can use `eval-after-load' to put in your .emacs,\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; will exchange the bindings:\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; (define-key paredit-mode-map (kbd \")\")\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; 'paredit-close-parenthesis)\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; (define-key paredit-mode-map (kbd \"M-)\")\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; 'paredit-close-parenthesis-and-newline)\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; Paredit also changes the bindings of keys for deleting and killing,\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; so that they will not destroy any S-expression structure by killing\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; or deleting only one side of a bracket or quote pair. If the point\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; is on a closing bracket, DEL will move left over it; if it is on an\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; opening bracket, C-d will move right over it. Only if the point is\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; between a pair of brackets will C-d or DEL delete them, and in that\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; case it will delete both simultaneously. M-d and M-DEL kill words,\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; but skip over any S-expression structure. C-k kills from the start\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; of the line, either to the line's end, if it contains only balanced\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; expressions; to the first closing bracket, if the point is within a\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; form that ends on the line; or up to the end of the last expression\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; that starts on the line after the point.\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; Automatic reindentation is performed as locally as possible, to\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; ensure that Emacs does not interfere with custom indentation used\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; elsewhere in some S-expression. It is performed only by the\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; advanced S-expression frobnication commands, and only on the forms\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; that were immediately operated upon (& their subforms).\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; This code is written for clarity, not efficiency. S-expressions\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; are frequently walked over redundantly. If you have problems with\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; some of the commands taking too long to execute, tell me, but first\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; make sure that what you're doing is reasonable: it is stylistically\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; bad to have huge, long, hideously nested code anyway.\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; Questions, bug reports, comments, feature suggestions, &c., can be\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; addressed to the author via mail on the host mumble.net to campbell\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; or via IRC on irc.freenode.net in the #paredit channel under the\r\n"},{"c":0,"s":";;; nickname Riastradh.\r\n"},"\r\n",{"c":0,"s":";;; This assumes Unix-style LF line endings.\r\n"},"\r\n",{"c":0,"s":"(defconst paredit-version 20)"},"\r\n\r\n",{"c":0,"s":"(eval-and-compile\r\n\r\n (defun paredit-xemacs-p ()\r\n ;; No idea I got this definition from. Edward O'Connor (hober on\r\n ;; IRC) suggested the current definition.\r\n ;; (and (boundp 'running-xemacs)\r\n ;; running-xemacs)\r\n (featurep 'xemacs))\r\n\r\n (defun paredit-gnu-emacs-p ()\r\n (not (paredit-xemacs-p)))\r\n\r\n (defmacro xcond (&rest clauses)\r\n \"Exhaustive COND.\r\nSignal an error if no clause matches.\"\r\n `(cond ,@clauses\r\n (t (error \"XCOND lost.\"))))\r\n\r\n (defalias 'paredit-warn (if (fboundp 'warn) 'warn 'message))\r\n\r\n (defvar paredit-sexp-error-type\r\n (with-temp-buffer\r\n (insert \"(\")\r\n (condition-case condition\r\n (backward-sexp)\r\n (error (if (eq (car condition) 'error)\r\n (paredit-warn \"%s%s%s%s\"\r\n \"Paredit is unable to discriminate\"\r\n \" S-expression parse errors from\"\r\n \" other errors. \"\r\n \" This may cause obscure problems. \"\r\n \" Please upgrade Emacs.\"))\r\n (car condition)))))\r\n\r\n (defmacro paredit-handle-sexp-errors (body &rest handler)\r\n `(condition-case ()\r\n ,body\r\n (,paredit-sexp-error-type ,@handler)))\r\n\r\n (put 'paredit-handle-sexp-errors 'lisp-indent-function 1)\r\n\r\n (defmacro paredit-ignore-sexp-errors (&rest body)\r\n `(paredit-handle-sexp-errors (progn ,@body)\r\n nil))\r\n\r\n (put 'paredit-ignore-sexp-errors 'lisp-indent-function 0)\r\n\r\n nil)"},"\r\n\r\n",{"c":0,"s":";;;; Minor Mode Definition\r\n"},"\r\n(",{"c":5,"s":"defvar","i":1198}," ",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-mode-map","i":1200}," (",{"c":5,"s":"make-sparse-keymap","i":1202},")\r\n ",{"c":5,"s":"\"Keymap for the paredit minor mode.\"","i":1204},")\r\n\r\n",{"c":0,"s":"(define-minor-mode paredit-mode\r\n \"Minor mode for pseudo-structurally editing Lisp code.\r\n\\\\\"\r\n :lighter \" Paredit\"\r\n ;; If we're enabling paredit-mode, the prefix to this code that\r\n ;; DEFINE-MINOR-MODE inserts will have already set PAREDIT-MODE to\r\n ;; true. If this is the case, then first check the parentheses, and\r\n ;; if there are any imbalanced ones we must inhibit the activation of\r\n ;; paredit mode. %s\"\r\n \"be careful of malformed S-expressions.\")\r\n (condition-case condition\r\n (check-parens)\r\n (error (setq paredit-mode nil)\r\n (signal (car condition) (cdr condition)))))))"},"\r\n\r\n",{"c":0,"s":";;; 4. nil if outside a comment, t if inside a non-nestable comment,\r\n","i":4538}," ",{"c":5,"s":";; else an integer (the current comment nesting)\r\n","i":4540}," (",{"c":5,"s":"and","i":4542}," (",{"c":5,"s":"nth","i":4544}," ",{"c":5,"s":"4","i":4546}," (",{"c":5,"s":"or","i":4548}," ",{"c":5,"s":"state","i":4550}," (",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-current-parse-state","i":4552},")))\r\n ",{"c":5,"s":"t","i":4554},"))\r\n\r\n(",{"c":5,"s":"defun","i":4556}," ",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-point-at-sexp-boundary","i":4558}," (",{"c":5,"s":"n","i":4560},")\r\n (",{"c":5,"s":"cond","i":4562}," ((",{"c":5,"s":"<","i":4564}," ",{"c":5,"s":"n","i":4566}," ",{"c":5,"s":"0","i":4568},") (",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-point-at-sexp-start","i":4570},"))\r\n ((",{"c":5,"s":"=","i":4572}," ",{"c":5,"s":"n","i":4574}," ",{"c":5,"s":"0","i":4576},") (",{"c":5,"s":"point","i":4578},"))\r\n ((",{"c":5,"s":">","i":4580}," ",{"c":5,"s":"n","i":4582}," ",{"c":5,"s":"0","i":4584},") (",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-point-at-sexp-end","i":4586},"))))\r\n\r\n(",{"c":5,"s":"defun","i":4588}," ",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-point-at-sexp-start","i":4590}," ()\r\n ",{"c":0,"s":"(forward-sexp)"},"\r\n ",{"c":0,"s":"(backward-sexp)"},"\r\n ",{"c":0,"s":"(point)"},")\r\n\r\n(",{"c":5,"s":"defun","i":4592}," ",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-point-at-sexp-end","i":4594}," ()\r\n ",{"c":0,"s":"(backward-sexp)"},"\r\n ",{"c":0,"s":"(forward-sexp)"},"\r\n ",{"c":0,"s":"(point)"},")\r\n\r\n",{"c":0,"s":";;;; Paredit is highly unlikely to work in earlier versions of\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; GNU Emacs, and it may have obscure problems in earlier versions of\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; XEmacs due to the way its syntax parser reports conditions, as a\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; result of which the code that uses the syntax parser must mask all\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; error conditions, not just those generated by the syntax parser.\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; Questions, bug reports, comments, feature suggestions, &c., may be\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; addressed via email to the author's surname at mumble.net or via\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; IRC to the user named Riastradh on irc.freenode.net in the #paredit\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; channel.\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; Please contact the author rather than forking your own versions, to\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; prevent the dissemination of random variants floating about the\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; internet unbeknownst to the author. Laziness is not an excuse:\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; your laziness costs me confusion and time trying to support\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; paredit, so if you fork paredit, you make the world a worse place.\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; *** WARNING *** IMPORTANT *** DO NOT SUBMIT BUGS BEFORE READING ***\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; If you plan to submit a bug report, where some sequence of keys in\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; Paredit Mode, or some sequence of paredit commands, doesn't do what\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; you wanted, then it is helpful to isolate an example in a very\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; small buffer, and it is **ABSOLUTELY**ESSENTIAL** that you supply,\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; along with the sequence of keys or commands,\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; (1) the version of Emacs,\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; (2) the version of paredit.el[*], and\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; (3) the **COMPLETE** state of the buffer used to reproduce the\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; problem, including major mode, minor modes, local key\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; bindings, entire contents of the buffer, leading line breaks\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; or spaces, &c.\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; It is often extremely difficult to reproduce problems, especially\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; with commands such as `paredit-kill'. If you do not supply **ALL**\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; of this information, then it is highly probable that I cannot\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; reproduce your problem no matter how hard I try, and the effect of\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; submitting a bug without this information is only to waste your\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; time and mine. So, please, include all of the above information.\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; [*] If you are using a beta version of paredit, be sure that you\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; are using the *latest* edition of the beta version, available\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; at . If you\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; are not using a beta version, then upgrade either to that or to\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; the latest release version; I cannot support older versions,\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; and I can't fathom any reason why you might be using them. So\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; the answer to item (2) should be either `release' or `beta'.\r\n"},"\r\n",{"c":1,"s":";;; The paredit minor mode, Paredit Mode, binds a number of simple\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; keys, notably `(', `)', `\"', and `\\', to commands that more\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; carefully insert S-expression structures in the buffer. The\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; parenthesis delimiter keys (round or square) are defined to insert\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; parenthesis pairs and move past the closing delimiter,\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; respectively; the double-quote key is multiplexed to do both, and\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; also to insert an escape if within a string; and backslashes prompt\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; the user for the next character to input, because a lone backslash\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; can break structure inadvertently. These all have their ordinary\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; behaviour when inside comments, and, outside comments, if truly\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; necessary, you can insert them literally with `C-q'.\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; The key bindings are designed so that when typing new code in\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; Paredit Mode, you can generally use exactly the same keystrokes as\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; you would have used without Paredit Mode. Earlier versions of\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; paredit.el did not conform to this, because Paredit Mode bound `)'\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; to a command that would insert a newline. Now `)' is bound to a\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; command that does not insert a newline, and `M-)' is bound to the\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; command that inserts a newline. To revert to the former behaviour,\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; add the following forms to an `eval-after-load' form for paredit.el\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; in your .emacs file:\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; (define-key paredit-mode-map (kbd \")\")\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; 'paredit-close-round-and-newline)\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; (define-key paredit-mode-map (kbd \"M-)\")\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; 'paredit-close-round)\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; Paredit Mode also binds the usual keys for deleting and killing, so\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; that they will not destroy any S-expression structure by killing or\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; deleting only one side of a parenthesis or quote pair. If the\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; point is on a closing delimiter, `DEL' will move left over it; if\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; it is on an opening delimiter, `C-d' will move right over it. Only\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; if the point is between a pair of delimiters will `C-d' or `DEL'\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; delete them, and in that case it will delete both simultaneously.\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; `M-d' and `M-DEL' kill words, but skip over any S-expression\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; structure. `C-k' kills from the start of the line, either to the\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; line's end, if it contains only balanced expressions; to the first\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; closing delimiter, if the point is within a form that ends on the\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; line; or up to the end of the last expression that starts on the\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; line after the point.\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; The behaviour of the commands for deleting and killing can be\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; overridden by passing a `C-u' prefix argument: `C-u DEL' will\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; delete a character backward, `C-u C-d' will delete a character\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; forward, and `C-u C-k' will kill text from the point to the end of\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; the line, irrespective of the S-expression structure in the buffer.\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; This can be used to fix mistakes in a buffer, but should generally\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; be avoided.\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; Paredit performs automatic reindentation as locally as possible, to\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; avoid interfering with custom indentation used elsewhere in some\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; S-expression. Only the advanced S-expression manipulation commands\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; automatically reindent, and only the forms that were immediately\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; operated upon (and their subforms).\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;;\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; This code is written for clarity, not efficiency. It frequently\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; walks over S-expressions redundantly. If you have problems with\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; the time it takes to execute some of the commands, let me know, but\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; first be sure that what you're doing is reasonable: it is\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":";;; preferable to avoid immense S-expressions in code anyway.\r\n"},"\r\n",{"c":1,"s":";;; This assumes Unix-style LF line endings.\r\n"},"\r\n",{"c":1,"s":"(defconst paredit-version 22)"},"\r\n",{"c":1,"s":"(defconst paredit-beta-p nil)"},"\r\n\r\n",{"c":1,"s":"(eval-and-compile\r\n\r\n (defun paredit-xemacs-p ()\r\n ;; No idea where I got this definition from. Edward O'Connor\r\n ;; (hober in #emacs) suggested the current definition.\r\n ;; (and (boundp 'running-xemacs)\r\n ;; running-xemacs)\r\n (featurep 'xemacs))\r\n\r\n (defun paredit-gnu-emacs-p ()\r\n ;++ This could probably be improved.\r\n (not (paredit-xemacs-p)))\r\n\r\n (defmacro xcond (&rest clauses)\r\n \"Exhaustive COND.\r\nSignal an error if no clause matches.\"\r\n `(cond ,@clauses\r\n (t (error \"XCOND lost.\"))))\r\n\r\n (defalias 'paredit-warn (if (fboundp 'warn) 'warn 'message))\r\n\r\n (defvar paredit-sexp-error-type\r\n (with-temp-buffer\r\n (insert \"(\")\r\n (condition-case condition\r\n (backward-sexp)\r\n (error (if (eq (car condition) 'error)\r\n (paredit-warn \"%s%s%s%s%s\"\r\n \"Paredit is unable to discriminate\"\r\n \" S-expression parse errors from\"\r\n \" other errors. \"\r\n \" This may cause obscure problems. \"\r\n \" Please upgrade Emacs.\"))\r\n (car condition)))))\r\n\r\n (defmacro paredit-handle-sexp-errors (body &rest handler)\r\n `(condition-case ()\r\n ,body\r\n (,paredit-sexp-error-type ,@handler)))\r\n\r\n (put 'paredit-handle-sexp-errors 'lisp-indent-function 1)\r\n\r\n (defmacro paredit-ignore-sexp-errors (&rest body)\r\n `(paredit-handle-sexp-errors (progn ,@body)\r\n nil))\r\n\r\n (put 'paredit-ignore-sexp-errors 'lisp-indent-function 0)\r\n\r\n nil)"},"\r\n\r\n",{"c":1,"s":";;;; Minor Mode Definition\r\n"},"\r\n(",{"c":5,"s":"defvar","i":1197}," ",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-mode-map","i":1199}," (",{"c":5,"s":"make-sparse-keymap","i":1201},")\r\n ",{"c":5,"s":"\"Keymap for the paredit minor mode.\"","i":1203},")\r\n\r\n",{"c":1,"s":";;;###autoload\r\n"},{"c":1,"s":"(define-minor-mode paredit-mode\r\n \"Minor mode for pseudo-structurally editing Lisp code.\r\nWith a prefix argument, enable Paredit Mode even if there are\r\n imbalanced parentheses in the buffer.\r\nParedit behaves badly if parentheses are imbalanced, so exercise\r\n caution when forcing Paredit Mode to be enabled, and consider\r\n fixing imbalanced parentheses instead.\r\n\\\\\"\r\n :lighter \" Paredit\"\r\n ;; If we're enabling paredit-mode, the prefix to this code that\r\n ;; DEFINE-MINOR-MODE inserts will have already set PAREDIT-MODE to\r\n ;; true. If this is the case, then first check the parentheses, and\r\n ;; if there are any imbalanced ones we must inhibit the activation of\r\n ;; paredit mode. We skip the check, though, if the user supplied a\r\n ;; prefix argument interactively.\r\n (if (and paredit-mode\r\n (not current-prefix-arg))\r\n (if (not (fboundp 'check-parens))\r\n (paredit-warn \"`check-parens' is not defined; %s\"\r\n \"be careful of malformed S-expressions.\")\r\n (condition-case condition\r\n (check-parens)\r\n (error (setq paredit-mode nil)\r\n (signal (car condition) (cdr condition)))))))"},"\r\n\r\n(",{"c":5,"s":"defun","i":1205}," ",{"c":5,"s":"enable-paredit-mode","i":1207}," ()\r\n ",{"c":1,"s":"\"Turn on pseudo-structural editing of Lisp code.\""},"\r\n (",{"c":5,"s":"interactive","i":1209},")\r\n (",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-mode","i":1211}," ",{"c":5,"s":"+1","i":1213},"))\r\n\r\n(",{"c":5,"s":"defun","i":1215}," ",{"c":5,"s":"disable-paredit-mode","i":1217}," ()\r\n ",{"c":1,"s":"\"Turn off pseudo-structural editing of Lisp code.\""},"\r\n (",{"c":5,"s":"interactive","i":1219},")\r\n (",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-mode","i":1221}," ",{"c":5,"s":"-1","i":1223},"))\r\n\r\n(",{"c":5,"s":"defvar","i":1225}," ",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-backward-delete-key","i":1227},"\r\n (",{"c":5,"s":"xcond","i":1229}," ((",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-xemacs-p","i":1231},") ",{"c":5,"s":"\"BS\"","i":1233},")\r\n ((",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-gnu-emacs-p","i":1235},") ",{"c":5,"s":"\"DEL\"","i":1237},")))\r\n\r\n(",{"c":5,"s":"defvar","i":1239}," ",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-forward-delete-keys","i":1241},"\r\n (",{"c":5,"s":"xcond","i":1243}," ((",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-xemacs-p","i":1245},") ",{"c":5,"s":"'","i":1247},"(",{"c":5,"s":"\"DEL\"","i":1249},"))\r\n ((",{"c":5,"s":"paredit-gnu-emacs-p","i":1251},") ",{"c":5,"s":"'","i":1253},"(",{"c":5,"s":"\"\"","i":1255}," ",{"c":5,"s":"\"\"","i":1257},"))))\r\n\r\n",{"c":5,"s":";;;;
